Anti-Drug Movement in This City Continues to Expand Propaganda, City Public Security Bureau Obeys the Order of the Director-General's Office, Joins Party and Government Circles to Intensify Propaganda 100

The anti-drug propaganda movement in this city has been mobilized since the 10th. The police officers in the city have been working hard to conduct propaganda and persuasion in the gathering places of the common people so that the general drug-addicted citizens will turn back as soon as possible and avoid being caught in the net of the law. In a blink of an eye, the ten-day period is full, and the results are considerable. More than a thousand people who confessed to the public security authorities and asked for smoking cessation have been reached. It was originally scheduled to end yesterday. According to Director Ye of the Fourth Section of the Public Security Bureau, the National News Agency reporter said that the public security authorities in this city recently received instructions from the Anti-Smoking Director-General's Office to unite with all parties and governments in this city to continue to intensify and expand propaganda in order to ensure that the anti-drug decree penetrates into the people and that drug addicts wake up as soon as possible to avoid unnecessary sacrifices to individual lives. The future of the nation suffers losses.

Good Phenomenon in International Trade, Trade Surplus with the United States 101

The main countries in my country's international trade are the United States, Japan, Germany, and the United Kingdom. Since the implementation of the legal tender policy, the import and export trade between these four countries and China has been on the rise. According to the customs trade statistics report, my country's trade with the United States has turned into a good phenomenon of surplus over export. According to last year's January to September, the trade deficit between China and the United States was 25,877,000 customs gold units, totaling 45,163,000 yuan in national currency. From January to September this year, this trade deficit has turned into a surplus, with the amount reaching 1,876,000 customs gold units, totaling 4,425,000 yuan in national currency. Other than the increase of 5,057,000 customs gold units in my country's trade deficit with Germany, my country's trade deficit with Japan has decreased by 15,637,000 customs gold units, and the trade deficit with the United Kingdom has also decreased by 5,303,000 customs gold units. Looking at the above figures, the total amount of my country's foreign trade has a trend of reducing the trade deficit. The trade with the United States, Japan, Germany, and the United Kingdom, the main countries, not only reduced the trade deficit but also had a trade surplus. With the exchange rate and prices reaching stability, if the government and the people can work together to improve the quality of national goods and open up overseas markets, it is expected that in the near future, we will be able to achieve trade balance and turn the trade deficit into a surplus.

Labor Unrest in Cotton Mills

A Large Number of Male and Female Workers Sentenced to Detention Separately… A Total of Sixty-Five People… Gathering in an Open Space in Caoxiebang, Macau Road, Apparently Planning Some Action, Detained for Investigation 103

Recently, labor unrest has been frequently occurring in Japanese-owned cotton mills. The Putuo Road Police Station, due to the concentration of cotton mills within its jurisdiction, has been taking strict preventive measures and ordering detectives to gather intelligence. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Detective No. 268 of the Police Station observed over a hundred male and female workers gathered in an open space in Caoxiebang, Macau Road, apparently planning some action. He immediately reported to the Police Station, which dispatched a large number of detectives to arrest them. Ma Guozhen, Wang Xiaosanzi, Liang Qingyou, Liu Jinle (all male), Zhang Adi, Lu Meimei, Zhao Jindi, Wang Jinmei, Zheng Caiyun, Wang Yueying, Zhao Meidi, Zhang Xiumei, Xu Linmei, Wang Caizhen, Han Jvdi, Gan Yingdi, Wang Xiuying, Li Amei, Wu Zhangdi, Wu Hanzhen, Zhu Gendi, Wang Guizhen, Zheng Xiuzhuo, Wang Advan, Gao Yufeng, Xu Xiaomei, Wu Shouzhen, Wang Yuzhen, Gao Miaoying, Chen Xiuying, Wang Xiaomei, Lu Xiaomei, Chen Xiaomei, Chen Guiying, and Xu Longying, thirty-five workers from the Japanese-owned Nei Wai Cotton Mill No. 7, who were on strike, were arrested. In addition, in nearby No. 51, Jiang Yueying, Song Caixia, Zhao Jvfeng, Zhang Dezhen, Wang Yingmei, Wang Amei, and Han Xiaomei, seven people, were arrested. At the time of the arrest, Jiang and others were beating Ni Caifeng, a female foreman at Nei Wai Cotton Mill No. 7, because Ni did not participate in their strike group. They were all taken back to the Police Station. At 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon, they were escorted to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The Police Station's lawyer, Qian Xunjiu, explained the case and, in accordance with Article 304 of the Criminal Law, requested severe punishment. After questioning by Judge Pan Xingyang, Jiang Yueying and Song Caixia were sentenced to twenty days of detention each, Zhao Jvfeng, Zhang Dezhen, Wang Yingmei, and Wang Amei were sentenced to ten days of detention each, Han Xiaomei was declared innocent because she was under fourteen years of age, and the rest were sentenced to five days of detention each as a warning.

Furthermore, at the Japanese-owned Shanghai Second and Third Cotton Mills, No. 1970 Yangshupu Road, after a labor strike occurred on the 8th of this month, it was quickly resolved. However, at 6:00 AM the day before yesterday, the labor unrest reignited. At the time, a large number of female workers prevented others from going to work and threw spindles, causing the situation to relapse into a strike. When the obstruction of work occurred, the factory immediately telegraphed the Police Station, which ordered a large team of detectives to suppress the unrest. Tao Xiaomei, Wang Jinfeng, Zhou Ada, Yang Xiangxiuzi, Zhou Lingzhen, Wang Xiuying, Yu Genying, Yu Gendi, Cao Linmei, Shi Linmei, Zhou Agen, Chen Xiaolai, Gao Gendi, Dai Qiaozi, Yang Gendi, Wang Zhaodi, Xu Xiuying, Wang Xiuying, Dong Xiaobao, Xu Biying, Wang Jinmei, Chen Xiuzhen, and Chen Guibao, twenty-three female workers, were escorted to the Fifth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court yesterday morning. The Police Station's lawyer, Jiang Baolian, filed charges under Article 305 of the Criminal Law for obstructing freedom. After questioning by Judge Zhan Liangce, Tao Xiaomei and others were sentenced to five days of detention each as a warning for jointly using coercion to obstruct others from exercising their rights.

Case of Japanese Sailor Nakayama Hideo; Yang Wendao Sick; Appeal Not Heard Yesterday; Notice of Postponement Given 104

Guangdong native Yang Wendao and Ye Haisheng were arrested by the police and brought before the First Special District Local Court in connection with the gun slaying of Japanese sailor Nakayama Hideo last winter. After several months of investigation, both were sentenced to death. Yang and Ye both claimed to be dissatisfied and appealed to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. A hearing was scheduled for the 20th of this month. It is now learned that Yang Wendao has been ill since being detained in the Xilao Prison in Tilanqiao. His condition is quite serious, and he has been transferred to the Public Works Department Hospital for treatment. As the scheduled hearing date arrived yesterday morning, the Second Branch of the High Court had been notified in advance of Yang's illness. At 5 p.m. on the 19th, because his condition had not improved and he could not be brought to court for interrogation, it was decided to postpone the hearing. The presiding judge of the criminal court, Yu Hua, notified the lawyers representing the two appellants, Yang and Ye, and the police lawyer of the reason for the postponement. Therefore, the hearing did not take place yesterday morning, and the future hearing date will have to wait until Yang recovers. It is currently difficult to predict.

The Chinese National Goods Production and Sales Association hosted a banquet for the press at the Hua'an Hotel at 7 p.m. last night. Finally, Qian Cangshuo, Pan Yangyao, and others delivered speeches in succession. The guests and hosts parted in joy at about 9 p.m.

Horticultural Exhibition Opened Yesterday 106

The third horticultural exhibition organized by the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau officially opened yesterday at the Pudong Donggou Agricultural and Forestry Farm (formerly known as the Garden Farm). Visitors were in high spirits. The exhibition area was decorated from the Donggou ferry terminal, along the way full of national flags. There was a horizontal banner that read "Shanghai Third National Arts Exhibition." Next to the entrance hung a couplet: "Beauty and wealth gathered in the garden, widely collecting all kinds of flowers in the same record, solemnly displaying art and planting, happily looking back to the beginning." The passage inside the gate was wide and spacious, planted on both sides with juniper trees, interspersed with various flowers. Among the greenery, red and purple competed in splendor, creating a refreshing atmosphere. In the western part, there was a shaded pergola, displaying various precious potted plants such as camellias, roses, and azaleas. In the center was a kidney-shaped pond, with a fountain above and fish swimming below, creating a unique and interesting scene. Turning west was a humble room, displaying exotic cacti, succulents, and begonias. Outside the greenhouse along the riverbank was a second gate, with a couplet hanging beside it, reading "Bamboo rhymes with maple red, vegetables and fruits compete for beauty, mountains surround water, pine and cypress flourish." Inside the gate, earthen hills stretched, flowers and trees thrived. Being in it, one felt like in a paradise. In the center of the exhibition area, there was a specially built thatched hall, named "Material Splendor," with a couplet beside it, reading, "Objects contend for novelty, scarlet, yellow, red, and purple, flowers and fruits flourish together, trees are planted and forests are vast." In the center of the hall, there was a plaque inscribed by Mayor Wu, reading "Exhaust the Land's Strength." Below, there was a terraced chrysanthemum slope, arranging precious chrysanthemums, with no less than several hundred varieties. There were also a hundred antique vases, filled with various chrysanthemums and wildflowers. Around the area were distributed the products of various companies, such as fruit trees, vegetables, local fruits, horticulture, and manufacturing tools, which were extremely exquisite. The fragrance of flowers lingered, and the fallen petals were colorful, making a spectacular sight. The prizes from various sectors that had been delivered included a pure silver "Award" shield donated by Mr. Du Yong, a silver shield donated by Director Lin of the Shanghai Municipal Audit Office, inscribed with "The Light of Agriculture," a brocade screen donated by Director Xu of the Finance Bureau, titled "The Joy of the Garden," a silver shield donated by Commander Ji of the Municipal Security Regiment, inscribed with "Proficient in Art and Planting," a shield donated by Mr. Zhao Shuyong of the Shen Bao, inscribed with "Old Farmer's Cold Fragrance," a package of books from the Zhonghua Book Company, a silver shield donated by Mr. Xi Guansheng, inscribed with "The Light of Horticulture," and a pair of silver shields donated by Mr. Zhu Dazhai, inscribed with "A Beautiful Woman Beyond the World, Silent Immortal." As of yesterday morning, there were over sixty participating companies, including the Shanghai Local Goods Industry Association, the Fruit Industry Association, Huang's Animal and Plant Farm, the Canadian Heating and Planting Farm, Bixia Garden, Lida Academy, Xiangshun Garden, Guanshengyuan Dahua Farm, China Chemical Industry Society, China Products Garden, Huang Family Garden, Shanghai East Art Chrysanthemum Farm, Shanghai Ferry Garden, Jinan University, Yisheng Seedling Shop, Nanyang Seedling Company, Asia Fertilizer Department, Potassium Fertilizer Company, Zhabei Charity Group, and Jiangwan Planting Farm. Outside the gate behind the southeastern hall, there were chickens from Lida, and incredibly large meat frogs. Inside the gate, there were rare goldfish from the Goldfish Paradise. There was also a special room for the Agricultural and Forestry Farm, and the Potassium Fertilizer Company Asia Company, killing agents, and many kinds of samples. Yesterday, there were several thousand visitors, with the people of Pudong accounting for 70% of the visitors. Today and tomorrow are Saturday and Sunday, and most people in Puxi are on vacation, so the number of visitors will certainly be even greater.

Overheating of Oil Vapor Caused Refining Pot Explosion, Injuring People; Ke Company Caused the Accident; Engineer and Female Worker Injured 107

Ke Lai Company, located at No. 410 Sichuan Road, specializes in shoe polish and other businesses. It has a factory at Nos. 307 and 308 East Jiaxing Road, and employs Zhang Rufa from Ningbo as the factory engineer. At about 11 a.m. yesterday, the factory owner, believing that a newly invented oil could also be made into shoe polish, but that the temperature required for distillation had to be higher than usual, instructed engineer Zhang Rufa to try it. He was instructed to increase the temperature of the refining pot to 120 degrees. Zhang obeyed the order. Unexpectedly, the pot exploded when it was subjected to excessive heat, causing the head of engineer Zhang Rufa and the face of female worker Zhang Wang to be scalded by boiling water. Zhang was more seriously injured. After the incident, the factory owner telegraphed the police, who dispatched a car to send them to the hospital for treatment.

Hong Shen, Owner of Hongfeng Tobacco and Exchange Shop on Gordon Road, Assassinated; Assailant Li Agen Admits to Revenge 108

Kuang Hongsheng, a 33-year-old Ningbo native, lived at No. 1182 Robert Road, Gordon Road, and ran the Hongfeng Tobacco and Exchange Shop. At around 11 p.m. last night, while Kuang was settling accounts in the shop, a man suddenly knocked on the door and burst into the shop. Without asking questions, he pulled out a pistol and fired a shot at Kuang. The bullet entered Kuang's left back, passed through his left chest, and exited, causing him to fall to the ground immediately, bleeding profusely. The assailant abandoned the gun and attempted to flee. Fortunately, Police Constable No. 1921 from the Putuo Road Police Station was on duty nearby, heard the gunshot, and rushed to investigate. Seeing a man rushing out in a panic, he knew something was wrong and arrested him. Kuang's family members also came out in pursuit, and after questioning them, the police learned the circumstances. They rushed the injured man to the hospital for treatment, while the assailant was taken to the police station for questioning. The assailant confessed that his name was Li Agen and that he and Kuang Hongsheng had worked on the same ship. He was fired due to Kuang's accusations, so he hated Kuang deeply. Today he came to take revenge and firmly denied robbery and murder. After obtaining the confession, the police detained the assailant, as the case still required investigation, and will send him to the court for trial this morning.

Two Married Men, Forcing Prostitution? Ji Wang Accused of Obscenity; Two Witnesses Fail to Appear for Interrogation 110

The afternoon before yesterday, a woman from Huzhou named Feng Baozhen (22 years old) reported to the Lao Zha Police Station that she had come to Shanghai on the fourth day of the eighth month of this year, as a guest at the home of her relative, Ji Wang, a woman from Huzhou, at No. 124, Tai Ren Lane, No. 49 North Zhejiang Road. Unexpectedly, the woman forced her to engage in a prostitute's life, accompanying her to the Dahua Hotel at No. 250 Beijing Road every night to receive guests. She was already married to a man named Feng Fachun, who is now at home in Xinshi Town, in her hometown. Because she could not bear the hardship, she requested assistance. Western Detective Crawford, Chinese Detective Yang Dechun, and Chinese Sando Head No. 1013, took Feng and rushed to No. 124 Tai Ren Lane and arrested Ji Wang. At the same time, they found another woman from Huzhou, Zhu Ying (22 years old), in the house. They learned that Zhu was also married, and her husband, A Jin, lived in Baibiao Village, Huzhou. She had come to Shanghai on the sixteenth day of the lunar calendar of this year and was induced by Ji Wang to become a prostitute. She had to hand over all the money she earned to Ji Wang. The detectives detained Ji Wang. Yesterday morning, they sent her to the Criminal Court 1 of the Special First Court. The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, stated the facts and prosecuted her for violating Article 231 of the Criminal Law. He said that Feng Baozhen and Zhu Ying wished to return to their hometowns and should be contacted so that their families would be notified. Ji Wang initially denied the charges, but after the police found tea waiter Luo Aweng of the Dahua Hotel and tenant Xu Chunxian of Tai Ren Lane to testify, she admitted to the charges. Today, although Luo and Xu were summoned, they did not appear in court. Next, the two women, Feng and Zhu, submitted a report of their experiences. When questioned, Ji Wang claimed that the two women voluntarily became prostitutes and were not forced, and that she did not receive any money from them. Judge Qian Hongye reviewed the confession and ordered that the hearing be postponed for a week.

Page 13

Lu Zhiqing's Career is Boring; Forging Keys to Steal Customs Declaration Boxes; Privately Engraving Seals to Steal and Sell Goods; The Case Solved Because of an Overloaded Rickshaw 111

Lu Zhiqing, a Ningbo native who previously worked as a clerk at the Minli Customs Brokerage, had a fanciful idea after losing his job. He manufactured counterfeit keys to the customs declaration boxes of the customs declaration offices and stole bills of lading to defraud goods. The case was discovered by Cheng Yongnian, a detective at the customs water patrol police station. The details have been reported earlier. The day before yesterday, he was interrogated by Detective He. Lu Zhiqing confessed that he was 22 years old, from Ningbo, and lived at No. 169 Hong'an Lane, Haining Road. Last year, he worked as a runner at the Minli Customs Brokerage. The company closed down at the end of last year due to sluggish business, and he was unemployed at home. On the fourth or fifth day of the national calendar of March, he went to the customs waiting room and used a brass key that he had found there in July of last year to try to open the customs declaration boxes. He had been an apprentice at the Yuxiang Public Association, so he knew that the key was for the customs declaration boxes and understood the procedures for customs declaration. He opened the No. 698 customs declaration box, stole a bill of lading for hat blanks, and forged the seal of the Gongxing Customs Brokerage, which was registered in that box. He printed it on the bill of lading and went to the Taikoo No. 10 warehouse. He hired a rickshaw, took out a box of hat blanks, and transported it to his home. He opened the box and found 30 dozen hat blanks. In mid-March, he sold them to the Hong Kong Cork Hat Company in Yangshupu through a buyer of old goods for 60 yuan, giving 6 yuan to the buyer of old goods and 40 cents to the rickshaw puller. From May to July, he studied acting at the Guiyou Drama Club in the Fu'an Amusement Park. Later, because there was no progress, he stopped and stayed at home to imitate the keys to the customs declaration boxes. Every day from 5 p.m. to 7 p.m., he tried to open the boxes in the customs waiting room. He made a mark on the keys and copied the box numbers and tried to find out the names of the customs brokerages registered in each box. Over two months, he made five keys that could be used, plus the two he found, for a total of seven. In mid-September, he went to the waiting room and stole a bill of lading for grapes from the Tongtai Customs Brokerage in the No. 682 customs declaration box. He withdrew 10 boxes of grapes from the Shuntai Yihua Wharf Warehouse, totaling 480 cans. Because there was no trademark paper on the outside, he could not sell them. He only gave the grapes in the cans to others and sold the iron cans to old goods stores. So far, he has sold more than 280 cans. On October 13, he stole a Finance Ministry cigarette transport license from the Meisheng Customs Brokerage in the No. 551 customs declaration box, and took it home. He saw that it was useless, so he left it at home. On the 11th of this month, he stole a bill of lading for lotus seeds from the Jingji customs declaration box (No. 741). He entrusted the Anli Transportation Company to withdraw 10 boxes of lotus seeds, but only five boxes arrived. When the car arrived near his home in Hele Lane, Haining Road, he sent them to his friend Hui Yongfeng's place (Huiheji shaft head workshop in the Chenghuang Temple Academy Road). He opened the boxes and packed the lotus seeds into four burlap bags and hid the rest in an empty coffin in Hui's house. Two days later, he and his friends Sun Zishan and Wang Yukang negotiated the sale of 1 dan (a unit of weight) and received 30 yuan in national currency. He paid off debts and redeemed things from the pawnshop and now has only 10 yuan left. The remaining passes were stolen by him in the customs waiting room during the last two months and have not been used. He engraved four fake seals, including Gongxing, Tongtai, Jingji and Wan Yu Tai. The seals of Gongxing and Tongtai had been destroyed by him. According to his confession, the accomplices Hui Yongfeng and Wang Libai were arrested. They confessed to the crimes. Witness Wang Kezheng testified that Lu Zhiqing went to his Anli Transportation Company to load 10 boxes of lotus seeds, so he sent a rickshaw to carry them. It was purely business and he knew nothing else. Rickshaw puller Shi Jiayao confessed that he loaded five boxes of lotus seeds. Because the rickshaw was considered overloaded on the road by the police, he hired a car to transport them separately, because the sea-ning road Hele lane would not accept the shipment. Because the time was too late, he had to send them to the Hongkou police station, thus cracking the case. After a thorough investigation, the police summoned four victims: Shen Liansheng of Jingji, Xu Yongkang of Tongtai, Dai Shaozhen of Gongxing, and Wu Baoheng of Meisheng. They also confiscated the counterfeit keys, a notebook, 33 passes, 10 yuan in national currency from the sale of stolen goods, three seals, three bills of lading, one cigarette transport permit, seven keys (three copper and four lead), and nine customs declaration box number lists. The defendant was sent to the local court for trial yesterday.

Xihe Third Factory Striked the Night Before Last; Labor Disputes at Japanese Factories Stalemate; Du Yuesheng to Serve as Mediator 113

Dagon News Agency reports that Du Yuesheng, chairman of the Shanghai Local Coordination Association, is to serve as a mediator in view of the fact that labor disputes at Japanese-owned yarn factories have been rising one after another, and the situation is trending towards expansion. This not only causes losses for both labor and management but also affects local security.

Situation in Factories in East Shanghai Eases

More than 3,500 workers at Shanghai Second and Third Yarn Factories, owned by Japanese merchants on Yangshupu Road Guangxin Wharf, went on a strike because the factory's promise to increase wages had not been formally announced and because the factory reported to the Grantham Road Police Station that 29 workers were inciting the strike and had been arrested. After many persuasion by the heads of various departments and classes, only 50% of the day shift (Class A) went to work yesterday morning, and 70% of the night shift (Class B) went to work. There are only six or seven hundred workers on strike. The other factories, such as Gongda Second, Tongxing, Dakang, Yufeng, First, Second, Donghua, and Shanghai First, Fourth, Fifth, and Sixth, are all working as usual, and the situation is very calm, and it is not expected to cause serious disputes again.

Xihe Third Factory Responds to Strike

The Xihe First, Second, and Third Yarn Factories, owned by Japanese merchants on Robert Road in West Shanghai, employ more than 3,400 male and female workers. The factory usually treats workers more harshly than other yarn factories, with daily work hours reaching 14 hours without any breaks. However, the factory has implemented a 5% increase in wages in response to workers' demands, but the 10% increase demanded by the workers has not been met, so they expressed dissatisfaction. At around 7 p.m. the night before last (the 19th), the night shift workers at the Third Factory first went on strike and shut down the motors. The workers at the First and Second Factories followed suit, and all work was suspended. The head of the meal workers at the First Factory persuaded the workers to resume work, so at about 10 p.m., more than 100 workers living in the factory resumed work. At about 6 a.m. yesterday morning, only more than 170 workers living in the factory went to work, but they were released at about 10 a.m. At about 2 p.m., the factory management visited Tan Baoshou, the chief of the Caojiadu Branch Bureau, requesting him to persuade the workers to return to work, and all disputes should wait for resolution. Director Tan and Inspector Gu persuaded the workers, and in order to comply with Director Tan's wishes, about 1,200 night shift workers went to work at about 6 p.m.

Representatives of the Three Factories Petitioned Yesterday Morning

After the workers of the Xihe First, Second, and Third Factories went on strike, they sent 18 male and female representatives to the Social Affairs Bureau at 10:30 a.m. yesterday to petition. Wang Xianqing, director of the mediation section of the Third Department, received them. The representatives stated the factory's usual treatment of workers and the conditions for demanding wage increases and requested assistance from the bureau. Director Wang inquired about the process in detail and stated that the bureau would send personnel to investigate the workers' demands and then find a way to handle them. The representatives left at about 11 a.m.

Dispatching Personnel to Investigate and Request Instructions on Handling

Yesterday morning, a reporter from Dagon News Agency interviewed Wang Xianqing, director of the mediation section of the Third Department of the Social Affairs Bureau, to inquire about how to handle the labor disputes at Japanese-owned yarn factories. Director Wang said that in order to understand the situation in the striking factories and the attitudes of labor and management, he would continue to send personnel to investigate the West Shanghai and East Shanghai districts. As for the handling of the labor disputes and whether to visit the authorities of the Japanese Textile Association in China again to discuss a solution, he still needs to ask the director for instructions before determining the policy. From the government's standpoint, he hopes that the labor disputes will be resolved as soon as possible to avoid losses for both parties.

Labor Dispute Inspections at Other Factories

(1) All 3,500 workers at the Toyota First and Second Factories, owned by Japanese merchants near the Zhongshan Road Bridge in Caojiadu, are still on strike. The Caojiadu Public Security Branch Bureau and the concession police have sent police to the factory and the surrounding roads to maintain strict security to prevent incidents. The Japanese have also sent armed marines to be stationed at the entrances of the two factories, and the situation is quite serious. (2) There are a total of 3,249 male and female workers at the Neiwaimian First and Second Factories on Robert Road. Since the workers in the Second Factory's cloth room took the lead in striking the day before yesterday, the day before yesterday, the workers in the First Factory had a conflict with the foremen, so all workers were released. Although the factory started work as usual yesterday morning, only more than 200 day shift workers went to work, and only 127 night shift workers went to work. (3) There are a total of more than 4,500 workers at the Neiwaimian Fifth, Sixth, and Seventh Factories on West Suzhou Road. More than 1,000 day shift workers went to work yesterday morning, but the number of night shift workers was reduced. About 120 workers in the Fifth Factory worked, and about 140 workers in the Sixth and Seventh Factories worked. Most of them were workers in the micro-cloth room. (4) Yesterday, two-thirds of the day shift workers and one-third of the night shift workers at the Neiwaimian Eighth Factory on Gordon Road went to work. (5) Yesterday, more than 200 day shift workers and only 147 night shift workers at the Neiwaimian Ninth Factory on MacKinnon Road went to work. (6) The Ri Hua First Factory on Robert Road paid wages yesterday afternoon, but the wages had not been issued to the workers, so no labor disputes occurred. All workers went to work as usual. (7) The workers at Neiwaimian Third and Fourth Factories at No. 19 West Suzhou Road, the Gongda Third Factory at Jessfield Road Xingjiapo Road, and the Tongxing First Factory on Gordon Road have increased their wages by 10%, so they have not been affected. All workers are working as usual.

Representatives of the General Labor Union Visit the Mayor

In order to resolve the labor disputes at Japanese-owned yarn factories as soon as possible, the Shanghai General Labor Union, led by its chairman Zhu Xuefan, Standing Committee members Zhou Xuexiang and Ye Xianggao, visited Mayor Wu at the Municipal Government at 10 a.m. yesterday. Because the mayor was attending a meeting, Secretary Yu was sent to receive them. The representatives stated the various situations and hoped that the Municipal Government would find a way to mediate to avoid the expansion of the labor disputes.

Key to Labor Disputes No Longer Local

Yesterday, a reporter from Dagon News Agency met a foreman working at a Japanese yarn factory and inquired about the labor situation. According to him, the treatment of workers in Japanese factories in China is too bad. For example, workers work for 12 hours a day, and there are no breaks during meals. While eating, they still have to take care of the work on the machine. If they are slightly careless, they will be punished. Now that the price of yarn is rising, the factories are making profits of tens of thousands or even hundreds of thousands a year, but the workers believe that it is difficult to maintain their lives, and the demand for increased wages is not excessive. If the factory does not agree to increase wages by 10%, then the workers can only go on strike to make the factory aware of the situation. This kind of action is supported by the general public in society. Now that the labor disputes have broken out, the factory should quickly formulate concrete measures and increase wages across the board, then the labor disputes will naturally be resolved. Otherwise, local wage increases will still be difficult to stabilize the entire situation. In this serious labor dispute, the Japanese should quickly withdraw the marines stationed in the factory to avoid escalating the labor disputes. Otherwise, any misunderstandings could create other unfortunate events, and the situation will be even more difficult to handle.

Special Precautions in East and West Shanghai

Two days ago, the police authorities in the Chinese Concession received information from various sources that the Japanese-owned yarn factories that had not yet gone on strike would implement a general strike starting at 6 p.m. yesterday, so they prepared in advance. The West Shanghai district was given special attention. The Public Security Bureau police stations along Zhongshan Road Bailinan Road, Gower Road, Robert Road, and West Suzhou Road increased the number of armed police, densely deployed posts, and patrolled. More than 100 Japanese marines were stationed at the entrances of the Japanese-owned yarn factories. Red police cars patrolled the roads. Two armored vehicles and a No. 25 military truck were parked in front of the Toyota First and Second Factories. The police stations in various districts of East Shanghai also increased the number of riding patrols and special patrols, and the security was very tight.

Japanese Side Cautious, Discuss Countermeasures

Osaka, 20th, Allied News Agency Electric Dispatch: The Japanese Textile Trade Association in China held an emergency committee meeting at the Cotton Industry Hall on the morning of the 20th. Based on the information from various factories, they carefully discussed countermeasures. As a result, the local headquarters of the association will be responsible for handling the matter in the future. However, the Osaka branch believes that the issue is quite political, so they must avoid provocative attitudes such as closing down all factories at once and should deal with it carefully.

Zhabei Temple Back Road: Black-Clad Robbers Wound Police Officer; Li Guoshun's Home Robbed, Vendor Reports to Police; Police and Robbers Exchange Fire, Xu Zhishun Shot Through Abdomen 114

Li Guoshun, age 42, from Dongtai, residing at 187 Temple Back Road, Zhabei, was suddenly visited by two robbers at 7:45 PM last night. The robbers, wearing black cloth jackets and trousers, each wielding a box gun, entered Zhu's house, silencing them and beginning to loot. As the robbers entered, a vendor recognized them and ran to report to the police on duty, who relayed the message to the Linping Road Police Station. A patrol officer was dispatched to surround and arrest the robbers. The two robbers, realizing they were discovered, grabbed over 20 yuan worth of clothing and jewelry and attempted to escape. They encountered the police and opened fire to resist arrest. The police officer returned fire, and the robbers fought as they fled, firing a total of over twenty shots, the bullets raining down like a string of beads. Third-class officer Xu Zhishun, number 2711, was struck in the abdomen by a bullet that exited through his back, rupturing his large intestine and causing profuse bleeding. He collapsed to the ground. The two robbers seized the opportunity to escape into Temple East Road and quickly disappeared. A suspect was apprehended nearby and taken to the station for questioning. The wounded Officer Xu was transported to Tongren Hospital for treatment, where his condition was critical and his life was in danger.

Thirty-Year-Old Woman Sues Seventy-Two-Year-Old Man: Where Does Xi Laichun Reside? Hangzhou Mail Returned; Xi Zhoushi Hires Lawyer; Court Orders Defendant to Appear for Further Interrogation 115

Nie Guizhi, a thirty-year-old woman from Yushan County, Jiangxi Province, has retained a lawyer to sue Xi Laichun, a man of seventy-two years, in the First Special District District Court for abandonment and other matters. She is also seeking alimony of 36,000 yuan. On the afternoon of the 11th of this month, Judge Huang convened a hearing, but the defendant did not appear. According to the plaintiff's lawyer, the defendant's residence includes 30 Jishan Lane, East-West Huade Road in this city, 21 Mashi Road in Hangzhou, and a villa in Qingdao. The court then ordered that the defendant be summoned for further interrogation. Previous reports mistakenly identified Xi Laichun as Xi Ehan, a wealthy merchant from Suzhou residing in Shanghai. However, the two Xis are distinct individuals and cannot be confused. This correction is made to prevent the spread of misinformation. Regarding the case, Judge Huang Risheng continued the hearing yesterday afternoon. However, the summons sent to 21 Mashi Road, Hangzhou, was returned by the post office as Xi Laichun was not there to receive it. Xi Laichun himself did not appear in court yesterday. However, Xi Zhoushi, from 30 Jishan Lane, East-West Huade Road, retained lawyer Jiang Yiping to represent her in court. Jiang stated that Xi Laichun originally lived in Hangzhou but had recently moved to Qingdao to recuperate due to illness. Lawyer Jiang also denied the facts alleged by Nie, stating that Jishan Lane has always been Xi Chun's residence and that the plaintiff's claim of cohabiting with Xi there is untrue. The court then questioned the plaintiff, who insisted that she was Xi Laichun's concubine, had been abandoned, and was in dire financial straits. She stated that if her livelihood were cut off, she would have no choice but to commit suicide by drowning. Judge Huang, noting the conflicting statements from both sides, determined that it was difficult to clarify the matter without the defendant's presence. He adjourned the hearing to the afternoon of the 27th of this month for further questioning.

Four Copper Coins for a Cake: Three Slaps, a Life Lost; Chen Shuxi Dies from Injuries; Lin Jinfu and Chen Cai Returned to Custody 119

Chen Shuxi, a 17-year-old from Yangzhou residing at 9 Renzhi Lane, Huade Road, went to Wanxing Pastry Shop at 949 East Huade Road on the afternoon of the 17th of this month to buy a cake for four copper coins. A dispute arose, and he was punched in the nose and bled by the shop owner, Lin Jinfu from Tongzhou, and Liu Cai from Guangdong. He returned home ill and was sent to the Sacred Heart Hospital for treatment. After treatment, he recovered slightly and returned home. Unexpectedly, his condition worsened the day before, and his father sent him back to the hospital for treatment. He died at midnight. The body was sent to the Feilun Road morgue for examination. Liu and Lin were arrested by the Huishan Police and taken into custody. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Attorney Zhang Shizhu of the Public Works Department stated that according to the victim's side, Chen went to Wanxing to buy a cake and had a dispute over the selection, and was beaten in the nose and bled to death by the two defendants. According to the defendant Liu Cai, Chen took advantage of the situation to steal a hundred copper coins. Lin Jinfu noticed and they chased him out of the store. In a nearby alley, Lin grabbed the boy's hands while Liu slapped him on the ears, causing the nose injury. Chen Rushi, the boy's father, stated that he was away from home when he learned that his son had been beaten to death by the two defendants for buying a cake. He asked for justice and kowtowed to the court. Questioned, Liu Cai admitted that Chen stole a hundred copper coins and fled. The boss Lin Jinfu caught him and Liu slapped his ears. He did not strike anywhere else. Lin Yu Fu stated that Chen stole money buying the cake, and he caught him in the next alley. Liu Cai slapped his ears, but he did not strike elsewhere. He requested the court to investigate. Judge Xiao Xiefen ordered them to be returned to custody and scheduled a further hearing. The body of Chen Shuxi was examined by Prosecutor Tang from the court, who determined that the deceased Chen Shuxi, male, died from injuries sustained in a beating. The body was handed over to his father, Chen Rusong, for burial.

King of Winter Melons: Weighs One Hundred Jin on the Market Scale 120

Mr. Feng Bingnan of West Shanghai has obtained a winter melon. While its size may not be as large as a five-stone gourd, it is rare among melons. It was displayed at the recent Sino-Western Flower Show, where all who saw it marveled and it won an award. It weighs around 100 jin on the market scale. Yesterday, Lu Bohong, Gu Xinyi, Huang Hanzhi, and Zhu Jilin attempted to lift it, but they could not move it even an inch. This shows its immense size and that it is worthy of being called the King of Winter Melons.

Guohua Cotton Weaving Factory: Carelessness in the Cutting Room; Workers Bravely Extinguish Fire; Losses of Eighty to Ninety Thousand Yuan 121

Guohua Cotton Weaving Factory, located at 861 East Youheng Road, produces cotton毛衫褲 and other items. It has over one hundred workers. The factory closes for rest on the 5th and 20th of each month. Yesterday was a holiday. Unexpectedly, a fire broke out in the cutting room on the third floor of the factory. By the time the watchmen noticed, the raging flames were already spreading outwards. They rushed out to call for help. Workers living near the factory gathered and used the factory's own fire-fighting equipment to put out the fire, but without success. At this time, the fire brigade also received the news and drove fire engines to the scene. They quickly opened the windows and poured water around the area, and the fire gradually subsided, avoiding a major disaster. However, all the cotton pieces in the cutting room were burned to ashes. The yarn-shaking room and weaving room on the second floor, as well as the cargo room on the ground floor, were flooded and suffered water damage. Machine parts also sustained considerable losses. The total loss is estimated to be as high as eighty to ninety thousand yuan. It is said that the factory has fire insurance.

Renji Hospital: Medical Report for Last Month 124

Renji Hospital's report for October of this year states: outpatient visits: 14,617; new inpatients: 305; inpatient days: 6,340; average daily number of meals served: 450; male suicides: 34; female suicides: 31; emergency surgeries: 382; emergency surgeries due to factory accidents: 56; patients sent by the Public Concession Police: 321; patients sent by the French Concession Police: 71; deliveries: 18.

The above statistics indicate that the hospital's work in October followed seasonal trends. The number of outpatient visits decreased slightly compared to the summer months. Among the patients treated, dysentery and similar illnesses decreased. However, the number of patients treated for malaria remained high, including tertian malaria. The number of surgeries due to factory accidents increased. However, it is fortunate that the number of suicide attempts decreased by 20%. The hospital is optimistic and hopes that this decrease is a sign of the general improvement of Shanghai's economy. In October, Dr. Hu Zhujun terminated his work at the hospital, which was a regret for both parties. Dr. Hu was responsible for medical affairs, especially in the hospital's surgical department, and worked with unwavering enthusiasm. What he received in return was only a small amount of travel expenses. Recently, Dr. Hu also took on the work of the women's and children's surgical ward, declining any additional compensation. Dr. Hu's departure from Shanghai to Guangdong was due to family reasons. The loss of Dr. Hu here is a loss, but it is a blessing for Guangdong. In October, two long-term inpatients were discharged. One was Mr. Zhang Yanxi, who suffered from chronic fistula and had been hospitalized for nearly five years. After treatment, his condition showed little response. As a result, Mr. Zhang saw an unfortunate patient come to the hospital and felt that he should give up his bed for that person. The hospital hopes that Mr. Zhang's decision will bring him good results after he changes location. Mr. Zhang is not yet able to work formally. The other patient who left the hospital was a child named Chen Qiaosheng. His departure was due to death. This child Chen was admitted to the hospital four years ago when he was only eight years old. He suffered from chronic hip tuberculosis, which later spread to tuberculous meningoencephalitis, which was the cause of his death. There is a story of generosity in this child's life that the hospital is eager to share. The child's condition, as described by Miss Xue Jisi, was known to the Poor Sunday School. Although the school was also materially poor, it was able to collect 6 jiao per day for the hospital expenses. The members of the school personally sent the money to the hospital. The Liverpool Sunday School also sent comfortable supplies. This act of kindness brought joy to this friendless and orphaned child.

Soochow University 30th Anniversary Special Issue

Our university is holding its 30th anniversary celebration and has received congratulatory inscriptions and artwork from leading figures in the country and sages from abroad, which are too numerous to include in this special issue. In addition to printing a separate special publication, we would like to express our sincere gratitude here.

Inaugural Address 134

— Liu Zhanen

Our university was founded six years before the founding of the Republic of China by the Northern and Southern Baptist Conventions of the United States. Through arduous pioneering efforts and painstaking management, it has reached its present state. The times have changed repeatedly, and reforms have been carried out one after another. The right to education has been managed by Chinese people for ten years. At the beginning of its establishment, the scale was simple and crude, with only dozens of students, a few teachers, and one school building. Economic facilities were extremely difficult to obtain. Today, on the banks of the Wusong River, we have purchased more than 400 acres of land, with buildings connected by clouds, and a magnificent scene. The number of students exceeds one thousand, and there are more than one hundred teachers. The graduates who serve the society have reached thousands. The affiliated middle school, primary school, downtown business school, Hudong Commune, and rural service center are also moving forward and developing year by year. All of this is due to the spiritual cooperation, hard work, and struggle of the teachers and students of Soochow University for the past 30 years. The assistance of all sectors is also appreciated!

Now, in order to celebrate the 30th anniversary of our university, the teachers and students of the entire school are publishing a commemorative album, the Tianlai Quarterly, and distributing commemorative special issues in various newspapers today, to show the people of the country, hoping to attract wisdom and effort. I think about the hardships of the past creation and the efforts that should be made in the future, day and night. There are several aspects that need to be developed urgently in the future of our university: (1) Develop various colleges, improve courses, hire more teachers, increase the purchase of instruments and books, and add departments as needed. (2) Expand the Graduate School, establish research institutes, sort out the existing research programs, and pay special attention to research in society, economy, international relations, and natural sciences. (3) Improve affiliated departments such as middle schools, primary schools, downtown business schools, Hudong Commune, and rural service centers. Within the scope of talent and economic possibilities, we will actively expand and enhance effectiveness. Furthermore, considering the complexity of the international situation, the changes in the social environment, the increasing foreign aggression, and the seriousness of national difficulties, how can we guide young people to fight against the enemy with the same hatred and revive the nation in order to achieve self-reliance? This is the major mission of our university in the future. It is hoped that alumni and students will uphold the spirit of universal love and sacrifice of our university, abide by the school motto of integrity, loyalty, diligence, and love; sleep on brushwood and taste gall, and be vigilant at all times, so that in this time of crisis and upheaval, we can shoulder the heavy burden, sacrifice the small self, and save the big self, in order to achieve the goal of our university of cultivating talents for the country. This is what I respectfully state in addition to celebrating the 30th anniversary of the school's founding, in the midst of joy and excitement. I hope that domestic sages will continue to guide! Earnestly promote! And add to the glory of Soochow University to the utmost.

Soochow University's 30th Anniversary Address 135

— Fan Zhengkang

Our university was established after many years of planning. It was founded in 1906 and officially opened in 1909. During the initial stage, Dr. Walter Russell Pettigrew, the first president, said in his report: "Our school has only been open for nine months, and the most difficult thing is the selection of teachers. This year, there are one or two teachers who, although learned, need to be corrected in terms of classroom management and student guidance. Unfortunately, one has resigned during this short period. The current problem is how to improve the level and complete the mission of our school." These few words are enough to understand the past policy of our school. Over the past thirty years, personnel have changed, but the policy has not changed. Last year's president's report said: "Our school has a considerable history since its establishment. However, today's success can only be called the beginning. We should continue to improve in order to realize the ideal of the founders." Thirty years have passed, but the consistency has remained the same. Our school has achieved what it has today, and we must remember the effective methods of teaching in the past. If there is considerable progress to be said, it is based on the achievements of the founding period, the so-called deep roots and luxuriant leaves, is it true?

Looking at the material progress of our school, what is worthy of praise is not the increase in school buildings, but the steps to promote the construction of buildings year by year, and the firm realization of the entire plan. Thirty years ago, there was only one classroom building. After that, buildings were added year by year, without interruption, all based on needs, planned according to needs, and realized by planning. Where there is a will, there is a way. This is what the past presidents can be proud of. Moreover, before each building is built, all expenses are carefully calculated, and construction is not started rashly until the funds are available. Therefore, the construction cost over the years has reached more than 1.097 million yuan by the end of last year, and there has never been any padding or borrowing. This is because it comes from free donations or is drawn from the accumulated surplus over the years. Only with a comprehensive plan and progressing on time can we have today's results. Here, we must recall the painstaking efforts of the executives of the past 30 years. In the future, the scope will become wider and the needs will increase with the times, but we will still adhere to the established policy and only wish to make gradual progress, not rapid progress.

Private schools often feel economically difficult, and Soochow University is no exception. According to the school's financial report, the first year's operating expenses (excluding construction costs) were 9,262 yuan, and ten years later it was 68,782 yuan, a difference of seven times. By 1929, it had increased to 282,545 yuan, an increase of five times. By the time of last year's total budget, it reached more than 340,000 yuan. The difference before and after is solid and far, but if we compare the progress that should have been made in 30 years at once, our school is still lagging behind. However, economic difficulties are a fact, and budgeting according to income is the only way for our school to cope with it. Whenever a budget is prepared, it must be revised in many ways until the income and expenditure are balanced. Therefore, since its opening, our school has not had the slightest loss. This is not enough to be proud of, because there are many things that should be兴 but have not been兴, and the feeling of having more than enough heart but not enough power is particularly painful. However, considering the future of our school, it is not enough to guarantee the future.

The number of undergraduate students over the years has gradually increased from 7 to 631, and the results are quite impressive. However, the average increase in the number of students in the entire school has not exceeded 50 per year. Except for a sharp decrease of more than 90 people due to the Shanghai War in one or two years, the rest have not exceeded two or thirty people. The so-called progress is gradual, and the decline is slow. In the past ten years, the number of freshmen has not exceeded about 200. Over the past thirty years, the number of students has gradually increased in order, which is gratifying. What is especially gratifying is the restriction of the number of students, so as to avoid the suspicion of emphasizing quantity over quality. As for the number of graduates in each session, from two to one hundred and eleven. Compared with the number of admissions each year (from 1921 to 1935), the highest percentage is 52%, and the lowest is 32%. In other words, only half of the freshmen in the first year can complete the program in four years and graduate. Economy and academics are the two major reasons. The former is due to economic difficulties, and dropping out of school halfway, and the latter is due to poor grades and dropping out or transferring. It is not easy to achieve the goal in four years and be worthy of the school's expectations.

"At thirty, one stands firm." Our school has reached the prime of life. All kinds of development plans after this are expected. Looking at universities in China, each has its own strengths, and the country's need for specialized talents is just beginning. Our school has a responsibility, and there are nearly a thousand graduates serving all parts of the country. How good their results are, the community will judge. However, how to cultivate students in school and in the future, so that they can be useful talents in the world and have a sound character, is something that must be taken into account. To sum up the achievements of our school today, in one word, it is steady progress. Steady progress is not rapid progress, nor is it slow progress, but a steady and active step to deal with the environment and plan development. In school affairs, we keep pace with the times, without being demanding or wasteful. In economy, we advocate thrift and use it properly. In teaching, we pay attention to basic knowledge and seek truth from facts. The world has quite a few people who find this commendable, so we state the facts in order to prepare people in the community who want to know the key to the success of our school.

Soochow University in the Past Thirty Years 136

— Zhu Rongquan

On the banks of the Huangpu River, the flowers and trees are lush, and three or five red buildings stand together, Soochow University is located there. It has been thirty years since its founding. In these thirty years, the hardships of its management and the beauty of its history are worthy of mention. Now, on the occasion of the 30th anniversary, I will briefly tell you about it.

I. The First Ten Years: The Founding Period

1. Completion of the founding plan: Twelve years before the founding of the Republic of China (1900 AD), American Northern and Southern Baptist missionaries stationed in China gathered in Shanghai to avoid the Boxer Rebellion, and the idea of ​​establishing a university in Shanghai was first proposed. Two years later, the two churches held a joint meeting in Hangzhou and Shanghai, and the decision to establish the school was made. Three years later, the Board of Directors was formally established. The following year (six years before the founding of the Republic of China, namely 1906 AD), the Board of Directors formally elected Dr. Walter Russell Pettigrew as the president of the university and Dr. Wan Yingyuan as the dean of the seminary, purchased 34 acres of land in Yangshupu, Shanghai, and built school buildings. Soochow University, which had been planned for a long time, was finally realized.

2. Progress of school affairs: The formal opening of our school was actually three years before the founding of the Republic of China (1909). At that time, there was only one building, Sihyan Hall, with only six teachers and seven university students and forty-nine middle school students. After that, school buildings continued to be added, teachers were hired year by year, and students also increased every year. By the time of the 10th anniversary in 1916, two new school buildings had been built, the number of teachers had increased to 26, and the number of students had reached 45 in the university and hundreds in the middle school. In 1913, the Hudong Commune was established in the workers' area of ​​Yangshupu, based on the spirit of social education, to benefit the poor workers. In 1916, the departmental system was implemented, and the scale of the university began to take shape. In these years, due to the initial opening, everything was kept simple. Those who were in charge of school administration mostly兼任 teaching positions, and those who were teachers worked hard to assist in school administration. With one heart and one mind, school affairs were able to prosper.

3. The first class of graduates: In June 1913, our school initially decided to hold a graduation ceremony. There were two graduates, one was Dr. Zheng Zhangcheng, who is currently the Dean of the College of Science and the Head of the Department of Biology, and the other was Mr. Wu Zhijian, who is currently a lawyer and was once the Secretary-General of the China Leprosy Relief Association. The two gentlemen have made significant contributions to Chinese science and social undertakings, and are also the pride of our school.

II. From Ten Years to Twenty Years: The Era of Development

1. Construction of new school buildings: During these ten years, the additions to school buildings included the gymnasium, science hall, McGaw Hospital, swimming pool, kindergarten, Syee Hall, upper middle school, and lower middle school. With more school buildings and complete equipment, school affairs became more developed. The former university and middle school, which were combined in one place, were also separated when the upper middle school was completed in 1922.

2. Implementation of the co-educational system: The co-educational system has long been popular in developed countries in Europe and the United States. In China, however, due to the excessive resistance of the old etiquette, it could not be implemented. Our school was the earliest and most vocal in advocating co-education. In 1917, this new plan was passed. In 1920, the first class of female students was enrolled. At that time, people in the community were stuck in old habits, and there were still few female students. Later, due to the promotion of the New Culture Movement, the atmosphere suddenly opened up. The implementation of the co-educational system in our school has gradually achieved results. As a result, schools that followed this system sprung up one after another, and the trend of co-education spread throughout the country.

3. Students' patriotic undertakings: On May 4, 1919, a student movement broke out in Beiping, and students in Shanghai responded to it. On May 30, 1925, the Nanjing Road Massacre occurred in Shanghai, the city was shocked, and the student movement was particularly fierce. It was often reported in the newspapers that other schools were suspended due to this trend. Our school, however, with a spirit of leniency, fulfilled its responsibility of guidance, striving to ensure that patriotism and studying did not contradict each other. Therefore, despite repeated trends, the strings of chanting were still the same.

4. 20th Anniversary: In June 1926, our school held its 20th anniversary celebration, showing its achievements in the past 20 years to the community. Our school is a latecomer among universities in China, but in the past 20 years, it has developed extremely rapidly, and at that time it was on par with advanced schools.

One of the School Scenes: Female Dormitory 137

III. From Twenty Years to Thirty Years: The Era of Innovation

1. The process of registration: In 1928, Dr. Wei Fuland resigned as president, and Dr. Liu Zhanen was elected as president and Mr. Fan Zhengkang as academic dean to implement the policy of Chinese administration of the school. The school worked hard to carry out registration matters. In 1929, it was ordered by the Ministry of Education to be approved for registration, and our school entered a new era.

2. New Development in the New Era: In this new era of ten years, through the efforts of Mr. Liu and Fan, school affairs have become more developed, and the number of students has exceeded the record every year. Latercomers were often rejected due to the full number of dormitories. New school buildings include the library, the middle school auditorium, and the female gymnasium. Under construction are Syee Hall and the University Auditorium. Most of the construction costs are raised in China, which shows that the educational achievements of our school have won the trust of people in the country. The number of teachers and students has also increased year by year, accumulating to this year, and even exceeding the records of previous years

Undergraduate Department: 57 teachers, 627 students (392 males, 235 females)

Middle School Department: 25 teachers, 400 students

Elementary School Department: 5 teachers, 140 students

Hudong Commune: 29 teachers, 752 students

Downtown Business School: 49 teachers, more than 600 students

3. Establishment of the Downtown Business School: Shanghai is the center of Chinese commerce, so the Department of Commerce is the most needed by the local area. Moreover, young professionals who study in their spare time are particularly troubled by the lack of opportunities. In view of this, our school strives to expand the Business School and add a night business school on Yuanmingyuan Road. In 1930, preparations were made. With the support of business leaders, it was formally opened in 1932. It has been five years now, and undergraduate courses, specialized courses, banking and accounting specialized courses, journalism courses, architecture courses, foreign language courses, and special courses have been added one after another. Over the years, the results have been well-received by people in the community.

4. Thoughts of Former President Wei: Former President Dr. Wei Fuland took over as president from Dr. Walter Russell Pettigrew in 1911 and resigned in 1927. He has been in charge of planning and management for 17 years, and has endured great hardships. Our school has what it has today, and Dr. Wei has made a unique contribution. His scholarship and morality have long been admired by all teachers and students of the school. After retiring, Dr. Wei continued to teach philosophy at our school until this year, when he retired to his home country due to old age. In order to reward Dr. Wei's hard work, our school specially built Syee Hall to commemorate him. Dr. Wei also wrote a short history of Soochow University, which describes the development of our school in detail. The materials are comprehensive and the narrative is detailed. It is an important publication of our school.

Education News

Key Officials of the Ministry of Education Initiate the Organization of the Chinese Normal Education Society and Issue a Circular Seeking Initiators 138

(Nanjing, 20th) Thirty-three people, including the Director, Secretary, Counselor, Specialist, Inspector, Section Chief, and Editor of the Ministry of Education, are initiating the organization of the Chinese Normal Education Society and are sending circulars to people across the country who have studied normal education. They believe that improving the level of education depends on the training of teachers. The reason why primary and secondary education in China has not been perfect in recent years is that primary and secondary school teachers have not been trained in the right way. In view of this, they are initiating the organization of the Chinese Normal Education Society. The tasks are outlined as follows: 1. To engage in research on normal education, such as investigating the actual situation of normal education, collecting materials, publishing books and newspapers, and studying and experimenting on various issues, are all important tasks of the society. 2. To seek to improve normal education, based on research results, to offer suggestions on normal education to the government, and to promote the reform of normal education, in order to establish a sound normal education system, which is the main task of the society. However, this event is a major one, and it is easy for everyone to work together. They will work together with those who are interested in normal education in the country. It is admired that you have made great contributions to the study of normal education. If you are willing to serve as an initiator of the society, we are looking forward to it. We hope to hear from you.

Director Pan's Speech

The Relationship Between Physical Education and Hygiene Education

Speech at the Municipal Physical Education School (Continued)

There is also one point. At present, the promotion of physical education in our country should not only be studied in terms of technology and methods, but also cultivated from living habits, because the rules of people's lives are closely related to hygiene. For example, daily living habits—that is, clothing, food, housing, and transportation—are disorganized, do not follow a fixed time, do not comply with certain rules, and do not follow ideal methods at all. Then, no matter how strong your physical strength is, it will definitely affect hygiene sooner or later, or even inevitably lead to illness. This school wants to become an ideal physical education school, so it is hoped that everyone will deeply understand the items of a new life that is neat, clean, simple, and plain, and practice them personally. I firmly believe that physical education and hygiene are both beneficial, and they "complement each other." Now I still have a little contribution, that is, I said above that physical education is a part of hygiene education. It can also be said that physical education is hygiene, but to talk about hygiene, it is not only from the physical aspect. We should also pay attention to "mental hygiene." In recent years, Western scholars have studied a lot about the theory of mental hygiene—especially in the field of education. Even in our country, a group of educators have recently been promoting it. Originally, a person's health is closely related to psychological mental activity. People's work certainly requires the use of limbs, but from a psychological point of view, it still requires the spirit to dominate everything. If there is something wrong with the mind, and something abnormal occurs, it will naturally affect the health of the body. You must know that the entire body includes "emotion" and "material" aspects. The material activity of the limbs must be directed by the spirit to succeed as a living person. If there is only an empty shell left, then isn't it a "walking corpse" and a "living dead person"? Everyone should see it more broadly. Both "mind" and "body" are included in the word "body." In the past, educational scholars advocated the distinction between moral education, intellectual education, and physical education, but this was only for the convenience of theory. In fact, how can the connection between "mind" and "body" be separated?

Today, I saw a piece of news in a certain newspaper, which was a dispatch from Tokyo, Japan. It said that a fruit store discovered that a truck had been stolen. The police chased after it on bicycles, but the thieves ran very fast. They only caught the thief, who was fleeing on foot, after chasing him for one or two miles. By then, the police were already very tired, but the thief seemed "very indifferent." Later, after investigation, it was found that he was the person who represented the country in international competitions a few years ago and broke the long-distance running record. Judging from this piece of news, it can very well prove that if physical education only pays attention to "special skills" on the sports field and does not work hard on the rationality and character of the mind, it will not only be useless, but may also inevitably lead to many malpractices.

Furthermore, let's talk about Shanghai. In some schools in Shanghai, students sometimes cause trouble. When investigating the troublemakers, it is found that most of them are athletes. Does that mean that athletes can flaunt their power just because they have good skills? Some schools have heard that student athletes can be more free and casual, even skipping classes and receiving special treatment. If this is true, it is too much. The school authorities think that they are the school's athletes and are representing the school to win honor, so they inevitably "worship them like gods," and they also regard themselves as "the pride of the people," doing the most intolerable things of bullying the weak and oppressing the few. If this is not changed for a long time, then advocating physical education seems to be too insulting to the true value of physical education. If principals or coaches treat athletes like this, to put it jokingly, what is the difference between raising dogs at dog tracks and raising horses at racetracks? This kind of rumored misconception must not be allowed to spread, because according to this statement, those who run schools certainly look down on the personality of others, while those who practice sports are also too unambitious. I hope that the Municipal Physical Education School must take the responsibility to correct this kind of wrong mentality and transform the atmosphere of the domestic sports world. Today, I have said a lot of miscellaneous words. I want to hope that the students of the Municipal Physical Education School will understand the national conditions of this country, see clearly the true meaning of the Physical Education School, and pay attention to the cultivation of living habits and mental hygiene at the same time in addition to physical training, so as not to fail the name of "physical education." (End)

Qinghua Football Team's Chen Rong

Today's Battle Against the Health Team

The Qinghua Football Team will play against the Health Team in the Western League B Group Championship this Saturday (21st) at 3:00 PM. The Qinghua team will use new and rising players to fight.
